      <p><b>Christmas Eve</b> is the evening or entire day before <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas Day</a>, the festival commemorating <a href="/wiki/Nativity_of_Jesus" title="Nativity of Jesus">the birth</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jesus_in_Christianity" title="Jesus in Christianity">Jesus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Christmas_Eve_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Christmas_Eve-4">[4]</a></sup> Christmas Day is <a href="/wiki/Observance_of_Christmas_by_country" title="Observance of Christmas by country">observed around the world</a>, and Christmas Eve is widely observed as a full or partial holiday in anticipation of Christmas Day. Together, both days are considered one of the most culturally significant celebrations in <a href="/wiki/Christendom" title="Christendom">Christendom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western society</a>. </p>
      <p>Christmas celebrations in the <a href="/wiki/Christian_denominations" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian denominations">denominations</a> of <a href="/wiki/Western_Christianity" title="Western Christianity">Western Christianity</a> have long begun on Christmas Eve, due in part to the Christian liturgical day starting at sunset,<sup id="cite_ref-Jerusalem_Center_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jerusalem_Center-5">[5]</a></sup> a practice inherited from Jewish tradition<sup id="cite_ref-Dictionary_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dictionary-6">[6]</a></sup> and based on the <a href="/wiki/Genesis_creation_narrative" title="Genesis creation narrative">story of Creation</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Genesis" title="Book of Genesis">Book of Genesis</a>: "And there was evening, and there was morning – the first day."<sup id="cite_ref-Genesis_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Genesis-7">[7]</a></sup> Many churches still ring their <a href="/wiki/Church_bell" title="Church bell">church bells</a> and hold <a href="/wiki/Christian_prayer" title="Christian prayer">prayers</a> in the evening; for example, the Nordic <a href="/wiki/Lutheran" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutheran">Lutheran</a> churches.<sup id="cite_ref-NE_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NE-8">[8]</a></sup> Since tradition holds that <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus</a> was born at night (based in Luke 2:6-8), <a href="/wiki/Midnight_Mass" title="Midnight Mass">Midnight Mass</a> is celebrated on Christmas Eve, traditionally at midnight, in commemoration of his birth.<sup id="cite_ref-Vatican_Today_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vatican_Today-9">[9]</a></sup> The idea of Jesus being born at night is reflected in the fact that Christmas Eve is referred to as <i>Heilige Nacht</i> (Holy Night) in German, <i>Nochebuena</i> (the Good Night) in Spanish and similarly in other expressions of Christmas spirituality, such as the song <a href="/wiki/Silent_Night" title="Silent Night">"Silent Night, Holy Night"</a>. </p>
      <p>Many other varying cultural traditions and experiences are also associated with Christmas Eve around the world, including the gathering of family and friends, the singing of <a href="/wiki/Christmas_carol" title="Christmas carol">Christmas carols</a>, the illumination and enjoyment of <a href="/wiki/Christmas_light" class="mw-redirect" title="Christmas light">Christmas lights</a>, trees, and other decorations, the wrapping, exchange and opening of gifts, and general preparation for Christmas Day. Legendary Christmas gift-bearing figures including <a href="/wiki/Santa_Claus" title="Santa Claus">Santa Claus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Father_Christmas" title="Father Christmas">Father Christmas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christkind" title="Christkind">Christkind</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Nicholas" title="Saint Nicholas">Saint Nicholas</a> are also often said to depart for their annual journey to deliver presents to children around the world on Christmas Eve, although until the <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> introduction of Christkind in 16th-century Europe,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> such figures were said to instead deliver presents on the eve of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Nicholas_Day" title="Saint Nicholas Day">Saint Nicholas' feast day</a> (6 December). </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_traditions">Religious traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Religious traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Western_churches">Western churches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Western churches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Midnight_Mass_2010_-_66_(5292245955).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Midnight_Mass_2010_-_66_%285292245955%29.jpg/220px-Midnight_Mass_2010_-_66_%285292245955%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Midnight_Mass_2010_-_66_%285292245955%29.jpg/330px-Midnight_Mass_2010_-_66_%285292245955%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Midnight_Mass_2010_-_66_%285292245955%29.jpg/440px-Midnight_Mass_2010_-_66_%285292245955%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Midnight_Mass_2010_-_66_(5292245955).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Midnight_Mass" title="Midnight Mass">Midnight Mass</a> is held in many churches toward the end of Christmas Eve, often with dim lighting and traditional decorative accents such as greenery
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholics</a> and high church <a href="/wiki/Anglican" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican">Anglicans</a> traditionally celebrate <a href="/wiki/Midnight_Mass" title="Midnight Mass">Midnight Mass</a>, which begins either at or sometime before <a href="/wiki/Midnight" title="Midnight">midnight</a> on Christmas Eve. This ceremony, which is held in churches throughout the world, celebrates the birth of Christ, which is believed to have occurred at night. Midnight Mass is popular in Poland (<a href="/wiki/Pasterka" title="Pasterka">pasterka</a>) and Lithuania (piemenėlių mišios). </p>
      <p>In recent years some churches have scheduled their "Midnight" Mass as early as 7&nbsp;pm.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> This better suits the young children, whose choral singing has become a popular feature in some traditions. In Spanish-speaking areas, the Midnight Mass is sometimes referred to as <i><a href="/wiki/Misa_de_Gallo" title="Misa de Gallo">Misa de Gallo</a></i>, or <i>Missa do Galo</i> in Portuguese ("Rooster's Mass"). In the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, the custom has expanded into the nine-day <i><a href="/wiki/Simbang_Gabi" title="Simbang Gabi">Simbang Gabi</a></i>, when Filipinos attend dawn Masses (traditionally beginning around 04:00 to 05:00 <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Standard_Time" title="Philippine Standard Time">PST</a>) from 16 December, continuing daily until Christmas Eve. In 2009 <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Vatican</a> officials scheduled the Midnight Mass to start at 10&nbsp;pm so that the 82-year-old <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Pope Benedict XVI</a> would not have too late a night.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A nativity scene may be erected indoors or outdoors, and is composed of figurines depicting the infant Jesus resting in a manger, Mary, and Joseph.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Other figures in the scene may include <a href="/wiki/Angel" title="Angel">angels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shepherd" title="Shepherd">shepherds</a>, and various animals. The figures may be made of any material,<sup id="cite_ref-Dues_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dues-13">[13]</a></sup> and arranged in a stable or grotto. The <a href="/wiki/Magi" title="Magi">Magi</a> may also appear, and are sometimes not placed in the scene until the week following Christmas to account for their travel time to Bethlehem. While most home nativity scenes are packed away at Christmas or shortly thereafter, nativity scenes in churches usually remain on display until the feast of the <a href="/wiki/Baptism_of_the_Lord" class="mw-redirect" title="Baptism of the Lord">Baptism of the Lord</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dues_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dues-13">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Whilst it does not include any kind of Mass, the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Scotland" title="Church of Scotland">Church of Scotland</a> has a service beginning just before midnight, in which <a href="/wiki/Christmas_carol" title="Christmas carol">carols</a> are sung. The Church of Scotland no longer holds <a href="/wiki/Hogmanay" title="Hogmanay">Hogmanay</a> services on New Year's Eve, however. The Christmas Eve Services are still very popular. On Christmas Eve, the Christ Candle in the center of the <a href="/wiki/Advent_wreath" title="Advent wreath">Advent wreath</a> is traditionally lit in many <a href="/wiki/Church_service" title="Church service">church services</a>. In candlelight services, while singing <i><a href="/wiki/Silent_Night" title="Silent Night">Silent Night</a></i>, each member of the congregation receives a candle and passes along their flame which is first received from the Christ Candle. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Advent2007candlelight.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Advent2007candlelight.JPG/220px-Advent2007candlelight.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Advent2007candlelight.JPG/330px-Advent2007candlelight.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Advent2007candlelight.JPG/440px-Advent2007candlelight.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="2703"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Advent2007candlelight.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Advent wreath, lighting the candle
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Lutheran" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutheran">Lutherans</a> traditionally practice Christmas Eve <a href="/wiki/Eucharist" title="Eucharist">Eucharistic</a> traditions typical of Germany and Scandinavia. "Krippenspiele" (<a href="/wiki/Nativity_play" title="Nativity play">Nativity plays</a>), special festive music for organ, vocal and brass <a href="/wiki/Choir" title="Choir">choirs</a> and candlelight services make Christmas Eve one of the highlights in the Lutheran Church calendar. </p>
      <p> Christmas <a href="/wiki/Vespers" title="Vespers">Vespers</a> are popular in the early evening, and midnight services are also widespread in regions which are predominantly Lutheran. The old Lutheran tradition of a Christmas Vigil in the early morning hours of <a href="/wiki/Christmas_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Christmas Day">Christmas Day</a> (Christmette) can still be found in some regions. In eastern and <a href="/wiki/Middle_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Middle Germany">middle Germany</a>, congregations still continue the tradition of "<a href="/wiki/Quempas" title="Quempas">Quempas</a> singing": separate groups dispersed in various parts of the church sing verses of the song "He whom shepherds once came Praising" (<i>Quem pastores laudavere</i>) responsively.</p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Krippe_Gutenzell.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Krippe_Gutenzell.jpg/220px-Krippe_Gutenzell.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Krippe_Gutenzell.jpg/330px-Krippe_Gutenzell.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Krippe_Gutenzell.jpg/440px-Krippe_Gutenzell.jpg 2x" data-file-width="903" data-file-height="742"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Krippe_Gutenzell.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A nativity scene
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Methodism" title="Methodism">Methodists</a> celebrate the evening in different ways. Some, in the early evening, come to their church to celebrate <a href="/wiki/Eucharist" title="Eucharist">Holy Communion</a> with their families. The mood is very solemn, and the only visible light is the <a href="/wiki/Advent_Wreath" class="mw-redirect" title="Advent Wreath">Advent Wreath</a>, and the candles upon the <a href="/wiki/Lord%27s_Table" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord's Table">Lord's Table</a>. Others celebrate the evening with services of light, which include singing the song <i>Silent Night</i> as a variety of candles (including personal candles) are lit. Other churches have late evening services perhaps at 11&nbsp;pm, so that the church can celebrate Christmas Day together with the ringing of bells at midnight. Others offer Christmas Day services as well. </p>
      <p>The annual "<a href="/wiki/Nine_Lessons_and_Carols" title="Nine Lessons and Carols">Nine Lessons and Carols</a>", broadcast from <a href="/wiki/King%27s_College,_Cambridge" title="King's College, Cambridge">King's College, Cambridge</a> on Christmas Eve, has established itself a Christmas custom in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-nine_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nine-14">[14]</a></sup> It is broadcast outside the UK via the <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_Service" title="BBC World Service">BBC World Service</a>, and is also bought by broadcasters around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-nine_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nine-14">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_churches">Eastern churches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Eastern churches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">

          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">

      </table> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2013-12-24--Artoklasia_during_Christmas_Eve_service.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/2013-12-24--Artoklasia_during_Christmas_Eve_service.JPG/220px-2013-12-24--Artoklasia_during_Christmas_Eve_service.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/2013-12-24--Artoklasia_during_Christmas_Eve_service.JPG/330px-2013-12-24--Artoklasia_during_Christmas_Eve_service.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/2013-12-24--Artoklasia_during_Christmas_Eve_service.JPG/440px-2013-12-24--Artoklasia_during_Christmas_Eve_service.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2976" data-file-height="3968"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2013-12-24--Artoklasia_during_Christmas_Eve_service.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Annunciation of the Virgin Mary Greek Orthodox Cathedral, Toronto, Ontario, Canada
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Rite" title="Byzantine Rite">Byzantine Rite</a>, Christmas Eve is referred to as <b>Paramony</b> ("preparation"). It is the concluding day of the <a href="/wiki/Nativity_Fast" title="Nativity Fast">Nativity Fast</a> and is observed as a day of strict <a href="/wiki/Fasting" title="Fasting">fasting</a> by those devout Byzantine Christians who are physically capable of doing so. In some traditions, nothing is eaten until the first star appears in the evening sky, in commemoration of the <a href="/wiki/Star_of_Bethlehem" title="Star of Bethlehem">Star of Bethlehem</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Christian_liturgy" title="Christian liturgy">liturgical</a> celebration begins earlier in the day with the celebration of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Hours" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Hours">Royal Hours</a>, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Divine_Liturgy" title="Divine Liturgy">Divine Liturgy</a> combined with the celebration of <a href="/wiki/Vespers" title="Vespers">Vespers</a>, during which a large number of passages from the <a href="/wiki/Old_Testament" title="Old Testament">Old Testament</a> are chanted, recounting the history of salvation. After the <a href="/wiki/Dismissal_(liturgy)" title="Dismissal (liturgy)">dismissal</a> at the end of the service, a new candle is brought out into the center of the church and lit, and all gather round and sing the <a href="/wiki/Troparion" title="Troparion">Troparion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kontakion" title="Kontakion">Kontakion</a> of the Feast. </p>
      <p>In the evening, the <a href="/wiki/All-Night_Vigil" class="mw-redirect" title="All-Night Vigil">All-Night Vigil</a> for the Feast of the Nativity is composed of <a href="/wiki/Great_Compline" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Compline">Great Compline</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matins" title="Matins">Matins</a> and the <a href="/wiki/First_Hour" class="mw-redirect" title="First Hour">First Hour</a>. The Byzantine services of Christmas Eve are intentionally parallel to those of <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday" title="Good Friday">Good Friday</a>, illustrating the <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_theology" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox theology">theological</a> point that the purpose of the <a href="/wiki/Incarnation_of_Christ" class="mw-redirect" title="Incarnation of Christ">Incarnation</a> was to make possible the <a href="/wiki/Crucifixion_of_Jesus" title="Crucifixion of Jesus">Crucifixion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Resurrection_of_Jesus" title="Resurrection of Jesus">Resurrection</a>. This is illustrated in Eastern <a href="/wiki/Icon" title="Icon">icons</a> of the Nativity, on which the <a href="/wiki/Christ_Child" title="Christ Child">Christ Child</a> is wrapped in <a href="/wiki/Swaddling_clothes" class="mw-redirect" title="Swaddling clothes">swaddling clothes</a> reminiscent of his <a href="/wiki/Burial_shroud" class="mw-redirect" title="Burial shroud">burial wrappings</a>. The child is also shown lying on a stone, representing the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Sepulchre" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Sepulchre">Tomb of Christ</a>, rather than a <a href="/wiki/Manger" title="Manger">manger</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Nativity" title="Church of the Nativity">Cave of the Nativity</a> is also a reminder of the cave in which Jesus was buried. </p>
      <p>The services of Christmas Eve are also similar to those of the Eve of <a href="/wiki/Epiphany_(holiday)#Eastern_Christian_Churches" title="Epiphany (holiday)">Theophany</a> (Epiphany), and the two <a href="/wiki/Great_Feasts" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Feasts">Great Feasts</a> are considered one celebration. </p>
      <p>In some <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox</a> cultures, after the Vesperal Liturgy the family returns home to a festive meal, but one at which <a href="/wiki/Fasting#Eastern_Orthodoxy_and_Greek-Catholicism" title="Fasting">Orthodox fasting rules</a> are still observed: no meat or dairy products (milk, cheese, eggs, etc.) are consumed (see below for variations according to nationality). Then they return to the church for the All-Night Vigil. </p>
      <p>The next morning, Christmas Day, the Divine Liturgy is celebrated again, but with special features that occur only on Great Feasts of the Lord. After the <a href="/wiki/Dismissal_(liturgy)" title="Dismissal (liturgy)">dismissal</a> of this Liturgy, the faithful customarily greet each other with the <a href="/wiki/Kiss_of_peace" title="Kiss of peace">kiss of peace</a> and the words: "Christ is Born!", to which the one being greeted responds: "Glorify Him!" (the opening words of the <a href="/wiki/Canon_(hymnography)" title="Canon (hymnography)">Canon</a> of the Nativity that was chanted the night before during the Vigil). This greeting, together with many of the <a href="/wiki/Hymn" title="Hymn">hymns</a> of the feast, continue to be used until the <a href="/wiki/Leave-taking" class="mw-redirect" title="Leave-taking">leave-taking</a> of the feast on 29 December. </p>
      <p>The first three days of the feast are particularly solemn. The second day is known as the <a href="/wiki/Synaxis" title="Synaxis">Synaxis</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Theotokos" title="Theotokos">Theotokos</a>, and commemorates the role of the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Mary" class="mw-redirect" title="Virgin Mary">Virgin Mary</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Nativity_of_Jesus" title="Nativity of Jesus">Nativity of Jesus</a>. The third day is referred to simply as "the Third Day of the Nativity". The Saturday and Sunday following 25 December have special <a href="/wiki/Epistle" title="Epistle">Epistle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gospel" title="Gospel">Gospel</a> readings assigned to them. 29 December celebrates the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Innocents" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Innocents">Holy Innocents</a>. </p>
      <p>Byzantine Christians observe a festal period of <a href="/wiki/Twelve_Days_of_Christmas" title="Twelve Days of Christmas">twelve days</a>, during which no one in the Church fasts, even on Wednesdays and Fridays, which are normal fasting days throughout the rest of the year. During this time one feast leads into another: 25–31 December is the <a href="/wiki/Afterfeast" title="Afterfeast">afterfeast</a> of the Nativity; 2–5 January is the <a href="/wiki/Forefeast" class="mw-redirect" title="Forefeast">forefeast</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Epiphany_(holiday)" title="Epiphany (holiday)">Epiphany</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Meals">Meals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Meals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Christmas_dishes" title="List of Christmas dishes">List of Christmas dishes</a>
      </div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Bulgaria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Bulgaria, the meal consists of an <a href="/wiki/Odd_number" class="mw-redirect" title="Odd number">odd number</a> of lenten dishes in compliance with the rules of fasting. They are usually the traditional <a href="/wiki/Sarma_(food)" title="Sarma (food)">sarma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bob_chorba" title="Bob chorba">bob chorba</a> (bean soup), fortune <a href="/wiki/Korovai" title="Korovai">kravai</a> (pastry with a fortune in it; also called <i>bogovitsa</i>, <i>vechernik</i>, <i>kolednik</i>), <a href="/wiki/Stuffed_peppers" title="Stuffed peppers">stuffed peppers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nut_(fruit)" title="Nut (fruit)">nuts</a>, dried fruit, boiled wheat.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The meal is often accompanied with wine or Bulgaria's traditional <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverage" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcoholic beverage">alcoholic beverage</a> <a href="/wiki/Rakia" title="Rakia">rakia</a>, in the past <i>olovina</i> (a type of homemade rye beer). The meals used to be put on top of hay, directly on the floor, together with a <a href="/wiki/Ploughshare" class="mw-redirect" title="Ploughshare">ploughshare</a> or a <a href="/wiki/Coulter_(agriculture)" title="Coulter (agriculture)">coulter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Czech_Republic">Czech Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Czech Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In the Czech Republic, feasting on the day of Christmas Eve (or only eating meatless food) is a medieval tradition. The belief is that if one lasted until Christmas dinner, they would see a golden pig, which is a symbol of luck. A typical Christmas breakfast is a sweet braided bread <i><a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1no%C4%8Dka" title="Vánočka">vánočka</a></i>. Christmas Eve dinner traditionally consists of a carp (baked or fried) and a potato salad.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="France">France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In French-speaking places, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9veillon" title="Réveillon">Réveillon</a> is a long dinner eaten on Christmas Eve. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>While other Christian families throughout the world celebrate the Christmas Eve meal with various meats, Italians (especially Sicilians) celebrate the traditional <a href="/wiki/Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic">Catholic</a> "<a href="/wiki/Feast_of_the_Seven_Fishes" title="Feast of the Seven Fishes">Feast of the Seven Fishes</a>" which was historically served after a 24-hour fasting period. Although Christmas fasting is no longer a popular custom, some <a href="/wiki/Italian-Americans" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian-Americans">Italian-Americans</a> still enjoy a meatless Christmas Eve feast<sup id="cite_ref-RachaelRay_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RachaelRay-18">[18]</a></sup> and attend the Midnight Mass. In various cultures, a festive dinner is traditionally served for the family and close friends in attendance, when the first star (usually <a href="/wiki/Sirius" title="Sirius">Sirius</a>) arrives on the sky. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lithuania">Lithuania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Lithuania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/K%C5%AB%C4%8Dios" title="Kūčios">Kūčios</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:K%C5%AB%C4%8Dios.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/K%C5%AB%C4%8Dios.JPG/220px-K%C5%AB%C4%8Dios.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/K%C5%AB%C4%8Dios.JPG/330px-K%C5%AB%C4%8Dios.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/K%C5%AB%C4%8Dios.JPG/440px-K%C5%AB%C4%8Dios.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:K%C5%AB%C4%8Dios.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Lithuanian Christmas Eve table with <i>kūčiukai</i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Lithuanian Christmas Eve blends pagan and Christian traditions as initially it was a celebration of winter solstice.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Traditionally, Lithuanians believed that animals could talk on that night, and it was possible to predict the future with charms and various games.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/K%C5%AB%C4%8Dios" title="Kūčios">Kūčios</a></i> ("Holy Meal") is the most important event of the year and family reunion. Dead relatives are remembered with an empty plate set at the table.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The feast starts after the rise of the evening star.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (December 2018)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup> No products made from meat, milk and alcohol are allowed during the Kūčios.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (December 2018)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup> In all, 12 dishes are served, all of them rustic, made from grains, fish, dried fruit or mushrooms including <i><a href="/wiki/K%C5%AB%C4%8Diukai" title="Kūčiukai">kūčiukai</a></i>. Small biscuits soaked in <a href="/wiki/Poppy_milk" title="Poppy milk">poppy seed milk</a> are served.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> After the dinner is over the table is left uncleared overnight for the feast of <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/v%C4%97l%C4%97" class="extiw" title="wikt:vėlė">vėlės</a></i> (spirits or soul).<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (December 2018)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Poland">Poland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Poland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Wigilia_potrawy_554.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Wigilia_potrawy_554.jpg/220px-Wigilia_potrawy_554.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Wigilia_potrawy_554.jpg/330px-Wigilia_potrawy_554.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Wigilia_potrawy_554.jpg/440px-Wigilia_potrawy_554.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1319" data-file-height="996"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Wigilia_potrawy_554.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Traditional Polish <i><a href="/wiki/Wigilia" title="Wigilia">Wigilia</a></i> meal
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A tradition similar to Italy (<i><a href="/wiki/Wigilia" title="Wigilia">Wigilia</a></i>, or 'Christmas Vigil') exists in Poland. The number of dishes is traditionally 12, but has been an odd number in the past.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> According to the <i><a href="/wiki/S%C5%82ownik_etymologiczny_j%C4%99zyka_polskiego" title="Słownik etymologiczny języka polskiego">Słownik etymologiczny języka polskiego</a></i> (<i>Etymological Dictionary of the Polish Language</i>) by <a href="/wiki/Aleksander_Br%C3%BCckner" title="Aleksander Brückner">Aleksander Brückner</a>, the number of dishes was traditionally related to social class: the peasants' vigil consisted of 5 or 7 dishes, the gentry usually had 9, and the aristocracy, 11 dishes, but the even number 12 is also found today to remember the <a href="/wiki/Twelve_Apostles" class="mw-redirect" title="Twelve Apostles">Twelve Apostles</a>. It is obligatory to try a portion of all of them. Some traditions specify that the number of guests cannot be odd.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In Poland, gifts are unwrapped on Christmas Eve, as opposed to Christmas Day. It comes from fusion Saint Nicolas's day (December 6th) and Christmas traditions. In the past gifts has been made on the Saint Nicolas's day morning.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="Russia.2C_Ukraine"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia,_Ukraine">Russia, Ukraine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Russia, Ukraine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Russia, Ukraine, traditional, meatless, <a href="/wiki/12-dishes_Christmas_Eve_Supper" class="mw-redirect" title="12-dishes Christmas Eve Supper">12-dishes Christmas Eve Supper</a> is served on Christmas Eve before opening gifts. The table is spread with a white cloth symbolic of the <a href="/wiki/Swaddling_clothes" class="mw-redirect" title="Swaddling clothes">swaddling clothes</a> the <a href="/wiki/Child_Jesus" class="mw-redirect" title="Child Jesus">Child Jesus</a> was wrapped in, and a large white candle stands in the center of the table symbolizing <a href="/wiki/Light_of_the_World_(Jesus)" class="mw-redirect" title="Light of the World (Jesus)">Christ the Light of the World</a>. Next to it is a round loaf of bread symbolizing Christ <a href="/wiki/Names_and_titles_of_Jesus_in_the_New_Testament#Bread_of_Life" title="Names and titles of Jesus in the New Testament">Bread of Life</a>. <a href="/wiki/Hay" title="Hay">Hay</a> is often displayed either on the table or as a decoration in the room, reminiscent of the <a href="/wiki/Manger" title="Manger">manger</a> in Bethlehem. The twelve dishes (which differ by nationality or region) symbolize the <a href="/wiki/Twelve_Apostles" class="mw-redirect" title="Twelve Apostles">Twelve Apostles</a>. </p>
      <p>The Holy Meal was a common Eastern Orthodox tradition in the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, but during the era of the Soviet Union it was greatly discouraged as a result of the official <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">atheism</a> of the former regime. It is coming back in Russia and continues to be popular in Ukraine. </p>
      <p>The main attributes of Holy Meal in Ukraine are <a href="/wiki/Kutia" title="Kutia">kutia</a>, a poppy seed, honey and wheat dish, and uzvar, a drink made from reconstituted dried fruits. Other typical dishes are <a href="/wiki/Borscht" title="Borscht">borscht</a>, <a href="/wiki/Varenyky" class="mw-redirect" title="Varenyky">Varenyky</a>, and dishes made of <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phaseolus" title="Phaseolus">phaseolus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cabbage" title="Cabbage">cabbage</a>. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Serbia">Serbia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Serbia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Candle_lighting_a_plate_of_oranges_and_smarties_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Candle_lighting_a_plate_of_oranges_and_smarties_1.JPG/220px-Candle_lighting_a_plate_of_oranges_and_smarties_1.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Candle_lighting_a_plate_of_oranges_and_smarties_1.JPG/330px-Candle_lighting_a_plate_of_oranges_and_smarties_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Candle_lighting_a_plate_of_oranges_and_smarties_1.JPG/440px-Candle_lighting_a_plate_of_oranges_and_smarties_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Candle_lighting_a_plate_of_oranges_and_smarties_1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Candles on Christmas Eve 2010
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Christmas_traditions" title="Serbian Christmas traditions">Christmas traditions of the Serbs</a>, their festive meal has a copious and diverse selection of foods, although it is prepared according to the rules of fasting. </p>
      <p>As well as a round, <a href="/wiki/Leavening_agent" title="Leavening agent">unleavened</a> loaf of bread and salt, which are necessary, this meal may comprise roast fish, cooked beans, <a href="/wiki/Sauerkraut" title="Sauerkraut">sauerkraut</a>, noodles with ground walnuts, honey, and wine. </p>
      <p>Families in some Slavic countries leave an empty place at the table for guests (alluding to Mary and Joseph looking for shelter in Bethlehem). </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gift_giving">Gift giving</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Gift giving">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gifts_xmas.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Gifts_xmas.jpg/220px-Gifts_xmas.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Gifts_xmas.jpg/330px-Gifts_xmas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Gifts_xmas.jpg/440px-Gifts_xmas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="565"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gifts_xmas.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Christmas presents under the Christmas tree
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant Reformation">Reformation</a> in 16th- and 17th-century Europe, many Protestants changed the gift bringer to the Christ Child or <i><a href="/wiki/Christkindl" class="mw-redirect" title="Christkindl">Christkindl</a></i>, and the date of giving gifts changed from 6 December to Christmas Eve.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> It is the night when <a href="/wiki/Santa_Claus" title="Santa Claus">Santa Claus</a> makes his rounds delivering gifts to good children. Many trace the custom of giving gifts to the <a href="/wiki/Biblical_Magi" title="Biblical Magi">Magi</a> who brought gifts for the <a href="/wiki/Christ_child" class="mw-redirect" title="Christ child">Christ child</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Manger" title="Manger">manger</a>. </p>
      <p>In Austria, Croatia, the Czech Republic, Hungary, and Slovakia, where <a href="/wiki/Saint_Nicholas" title="Saint Nicholas">Saint Nicholas</a> (sv. Mikuláš/szent Mikulás) gives his sweet gifts on 6 December, the Christmas gift-giver is the <a href="/wiki/Christkind" title="Christkind">Child Jesus</a> (<a href="/wiki/Je%C5%BE%C3%AD%C5%A1ek" class="mw-redirect" title="Ježíšek">Ježíšek</a> in <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>, Jézuska in Hungarian, Ježiško in <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">Slovak</a> and Isusek in <a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">Croatian</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In most parts of Austria, the Czech Republic, Germany, Hungary, Poland, Slovakia, and Switzerland, presents are traditionally exchanged on the evening of 24 December. Children are commonly told that presents were brought either by the <a href="/wiki/Christkind" title="Christkind">Christkind</a> (German for Christ child),<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> or by the <a href="/wiki/Weihnachtsmann" class="mw-redirect" title="Weihnachtsmann">Weihnachtsmann</a>. Both leave the gifts, but are in most families not seen doing so. In Germany, the gifts are also brought on 6 December by "the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Nicholas" title="Saint Nicholas">Nikolaus</a>" with his helper <a href="/wiki/Knecht_Ruprecht" title="Knecht Ruprecht">Knecht Ruprecht</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gezin_bij_de_kerstboom_c1860.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Gezin_bij_de_kerstboom_c1860.jpg/220px-Gezin_bij_de_kerstboom_c1860.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Gezin_bij_de_kerstboom_c1860.jpg/330px-Gezin_bij_de_kerstboom_c1860.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Gezin_bij_de_kerstboom_c1860.jpg/440px-Gezin_bij_de_kerstboom_c1860.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="562"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gezin_bij_de_kerstboom_c1860.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Christmas tree with presents hanging on the tree
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In Estonia <i><a href="/wiki/J%C3%B5uluvana" class="mw-redirect" title="Jõuluvana">Jõuluvana</a></i>, Finland <i><a href="/wiki/Joulupukki" title="Joulupukki">Joulupukki</a></i>, Denmark <i><a href="/wiki/Julemanden" title="Julemanden">Julemanden</a></i>, Norway <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Julenissen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Julenissen (page does not exist)">Julenissen</a></i> and Sweden <i><a href="/wiki/Jultomten" class="mw-redirect" title="Jultomten">Jultomten</a></i>, personally meets children and gives presents in the evening of Christmas Eve.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In Argentina, Austria, Brazil, Colombia, Denmark, Estonia, the Faroe Islands, Finland, France, Germany, Hungary, Iceland, Latvia, Lithuania, Luxembourg, Norway, Poland, Portugal, French Canada, Romania, Uruguay, Slovakia, Slovenia, Sweden, Switzerland and the Czech Republic, Christmas presents are opened mostly on the evening of the 24th – following German tradition, this is also the practice among the <a href="/wiki/British_Royal_Family" class="mw-redirect" title="British Royal Family">British Royal Family</a> since it was introduced by <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albert,_Prince_Consort" title="Albert, Prince Consort">Albert, Prince Consort</a><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> – while in Italy, the United States, the United Kingdom, Republic of Ireland, English Canada, South Africa, New Zealand and Australia, this occurs mostly on the morning of Christmas Day. </p>
      <p>In other Latin American countries, people stay awake until <a href="/wiki/Midnight" title="Midnight">midnight</a>, when they open the presents. </p>
      <p>In Spain, gifts are traditionally opened on the morning of 6 January, <a href="/wiki/Epiphany_(feast)" class="mw-redirect" title="Epiphany (feast)">Epiphany day</a> ("Día de Los Tres Reyes Magos"),<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> though in some other countries, like Mexico, Argentina and Uruguay, people receive presents both around Christmas and on the morning of <a href="/wiki/Epiphany_(holiday)" title="Epiphany (holiday)">Epiphany</a> day. </p>
      <p>In Belgium and the Netherlands <a href="/wiki/Saint_Nicholas" title="Saint Nicholas">Saint Nicholas</a> or <a href="/wiki/Sinterklaas" title="Sinterklaas">Sinterklaas</a> and his companion <a href="/wiki/Zwarte_Piet" title="Zwarte Piet">Zwarte Piet</a> deliver presents to children and adults alike on the evening of 5 December, the eve of his nameday.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> On 24 December they go to church or watch the late-night Mass on TV, or have a meal.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Christmas_Eve_around_the_world">Christmas Eve around the world</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Christmas Eve around the world">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_The_U.S._Army_-_Christmas_Eve_Candlelight_Services.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Flickr_-_The_U.S._Army_-_Christmas_Eve_Candlelight_Services.jpg/220px-Flickr_-_The_U.S._Army_-_Christmas_Eve_Candlelight_Services.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Flickr_-_The_U.S._Army_-_Christmas_Eve_Candlelight_Services.jpg/330px-Flickr_-_The_U.S._Army_-_Christmas_Eve_Candlelight_Services.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Flickr_-_The_U.S._Army_-_Christmas_Eve_Candlelight_Services.jpg/440px-Flickr_-_The_U.S._Army_-_Christmas_Eve_Candlelight_Services.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2819" data-file-height="1879"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_The_U.S._Army_-_Christmas_Eve_Candlelight_Services.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Christmas Eve candlelight <a href="/wiki/Service_of_worship" class="mw-redirect" title="Service of worship">service</a> in <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>, Iraq
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Christmas Eve is celebrated in different ways around the world, varying by country and region. Elements common to many areas of the world include the attendance of special religious observances such as a midnight Mass or Vespers and the giving and receiving of presents. Along with Easter, Christmastime is one of the most important periods on the Christian calendar, and is often closely connected to other holidays at this time of year, such as Advent, the Feast of the Immaculate Conception, St. Nicholas Day, St. Stephen's Day, New Year's, and the Feast of the Epiphany. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Celebrations">Celebrations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Celebrations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Among Christians, as well as non-Christians who celebrate Christmas, the significant amount of vacation travel, and travel back to family homes, that takes place in the lead-up to Christmas means that Christmas Eve is also frequently a time of social events and parties, worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-Fodor_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fodor-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Discourse_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Discourse-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Culture_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Culture-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tonic_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tonic-41">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ohio_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ohio-42">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information on Christmas Eve traditions around the world: <a href="/wiki/Christmas_worldwide" class="mw-redirect" title="Christmas worldwide">Christmas worldwide</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_Jewish_culture">In Jewish culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: In Jewish culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Nittel_Nacht" title="Nittel Nacht">Nittel Nacht</a> is a name given to Christmas Eve by Jewish scholars in the 17th century. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="In_contemporary_American-Jewish_culture">In contemporary American-Jewish culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: In contemporary American-Jewish culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>With Christmas Day a <a href="/wiki/Work_holiday" class="mw-redirect" title="Work holiday">work holiday</a> throughout the United States, there is a space of unfilled free time during which much of American commerce and society is not functioning, and which can give rise to a sense of loneliness or alienation for American Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-Hwang_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hwang-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AP2006_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP2006-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tracy_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tracy-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lewis_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ChinaDaily_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChinaDaily-47">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Jews also typically do not engage in the family gathering and religious worship activities that are central to Christmas Eve for Christians.<sup id="cite_ref-TimesDeciding_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TimesDeciding-48">[48]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Typical contemporary activities have usually been limited to "Chinese and a movie"<sup id="cite_ref-Karch_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Karch-49">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wiener_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wiener-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Vozick_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vozick-51">[51]</a></sup>—consuming a meal at a <a href="/wiki/Chinese_restaurant" title="Chinese restaurant">Chinese restaurant</a>, which tend to be open for business on the Christmas holiday, and watching a movie at the theater or at home, stereotypically a rerun of <i><a href="/wiki/It%27s_a_Wonderful_Life" title="It's a Wonderful Life">It's a Wonderful Life</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-ChinaDaily_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChinaDaily-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Heyman2010_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heyman2010-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Duckett_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Duckett-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gluck_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gluck-54">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since the 1980s a variety of social events for young Jews have sprung up, and become popular, on Christmas Eve.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-55">[55]</a></sup> These include the <a href="/wiki/Matzo_Ball" title="Matzo Ball">Matzo Ball</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Ball_(event)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Ball (event)">The Ball</a>, and a number of local events organized by Jewish communities and <a href="/wiki/Local_Jewish_Federations" class="mw-redirect" title="Local Jewish Federations">local Jewish Federations</a> in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-AP2006_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP2006-44">[44]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information on Christmas Eve social events for young Jews in North America: <a href="/wiki/Matzo_Ball" title="Matzo Ball">Matzo Ball</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_Chinese_culture">In Chinese culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: In Chinese culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In Mandarin, Christmas Eve is called <i lang="zh-Latn" title="Chinese-language romanization">Píng'ān yè</i> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese-language text">平安夜</span>, "peaceful night", etymologically from the Chinese title of the Christmas carol <i><a href="/wiki/Silent_Night" title="Silent Night">Silent Night</a></i>). People exchange apples, because the word for "apple" (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r976166364">.mw-parser-output ruby>rt,.mw-parser-output ruby>rtc{font-feature-settings:"ruby"1;font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output ruby.large{font-size:250%}.mw-parser-output ruby.large>rt,.mw-parser-output ruby.large>rtc{font-size:50%}</style><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r998571036">.mw-parser-output .ruby-zh-p>rt{font-family:"Arial Unicode MS","Bitstream Cyberbit","TITUS Cyberbit Basic","Lucida Sans Unicode",inherit}</style><ruby lang="Zh-Hans" class="ruby-zh-p">
        <rb>
         <span lang="zh" title="Chinese-language text">苹</span>
        </rb><rp>(</rp><rt class="pinyin"><span style="font-style: normal" lang="zh-Latn" title="ISO 7098 Chinese (Chinese language) transliteration">píng</span></rt><rp>)</rp></ruby>果) is a rhyming wordplay with "peace" (
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r976166364">
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r998571036"><ruby lang="Zh-Hans" class="ruby-zh-p">
        <rb>
         <span lang="zh" title="Chinese-language text">平</span>
        </rb><rp>(</rp><rt class="pinyin"><span style="font-style: normal" lang="zh-Latn" title="ISO 7098 Chinese (Chinese language) transliteration">píng</span></rt><rp>)</rp></ruby>安).<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_Inuit_culture">In Inuit culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: In Inuit culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a> territories, Christmas Eve is called <i><a href="/wiki/Quviasukvik" title="Quviasukvik">Quviasukvik</a></i>. The Inuit celebrate it as their new year.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_events">Historical events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Historical events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Khaki-chums-xmas-truce-1914-1999.redvers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Khaki-chums-xmas-truce-1914-1999.redvers.jpg/220px-Khaki-chums-xmas-truce-1914-1999.redvers.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Khaki-chums-xmas-truce-1914-1999.redvers.jpg/330px-Khaki-chums-xmas-truce-1914-1999.redvers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Khaki-chums-xmas-truce-1914-1999.redvers.jpg/440px-Khaki-chums-xmas-truce-1914-1999.redvers.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="975"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Khaki-chums-xmas-truce-1914-1999.redvers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A cross, left near <a href="/wiki/Ypres" title="Ypres">Ypres</a> in Belgium in 1999, to commemorate the site of the 1914 Christmas Truce. The text reads <i>1914—The Khaki Chum's Christmas Truce—85 Years—Lest We Forget</i>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A number of historical events have been influenced by the occurrence of Christmas Eve. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Christmas_truce">Christmas truce</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Christmas truce">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Christmas_truce" title="Christmas truce">Christmas truce</a>
      </div> 
      <p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> in 1914 and 1915 there was an unofficial <a href="/wiki/Christmas_truce" title="Christmas truce">Christmas truce</a>, particularly between <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">British</a> and <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German</a> troops. The truce began on Christmas Eve, 24 December 1914, when <a href="/wiki/German_Army_(German_Empire)" title="German Army (German Empire)">German troops</a> began decorating the area around their <a href="/wiki/Trench_warfare" title="Trench warfare">trenches</a> in the region of <a href="/wiki/Ypres" title="Ypres">Ypres</a>, Belgium, for Christmas. They began by placing candles on trees, then continued the celebration by singing <a href="/wiki/Christmas_carol" title="Christmas carol">Christmas carols</a>, most notably <i><a href="/wiki/Silent_Night_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Silent Night (song)">Stille Nacht</a></i> ("Silent Night"). The <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British troops</a> in the trenches across from them responded by singing English carols. The two sides shouted Christmas greetings to each other. Soon there were calls for visits across the "<a href="/wiki/No_man%27s_land" title="No man's land">No man's land</a>" when small gifts were exchanged. The truce also allowed a breathing space during which recently killed soldiers could be brought back behind their lines by burial parties. Funerals took place as soldiers from both sides mourned the dead together and paid their respects. At one funeral in No Man's Land, soldiers from both sides gathered and read a passage from <a href="/wiki/Psalm_23" title="Psalm 23">Psalm 23</a>. The truce occurred in spite of opposition at higher levels of the military command. Earlier in the autumn, a call by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XV" title="Pope Benedict XV">Pope Benedict XV</a> for an official truce between the warring governments had been ignored. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:NASA-Apollo8-Dec24-Earthrise.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/NASA-Apollo8-Dec24-Earthrise.jpg/220px-NASA-Apollo8-Dec24-Earthrise.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/NASA-Apollo8-Dec24-Earthrise.jpg/330px-NASA-Apollo8-Dec24-Earthrise.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/NASA-Apollo8-Dec24-Earthrise.jpg/440px-NASA-Apollo8-Dec24-Earthrise.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="2400"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:NASA-Apollo8-Dec24-Earthrise.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i><a href="/wiki/Earthrise" title="Earthrise">Earthrise</a></i>, as seen from <a href="/wiki/Apollo_8" title="Apollo 8">Apollo 8</a>, 24 December 1968, photographed by astronaut <a href="/wiki/William_Anders" title="William Anders">William Anders</a> (<a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Apollo_8_reading_from_Genesis">Apollo 8 reading from Genesis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Apollo 8 reading from Genesis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Apollo_8_Genesis_reading" title="Apollo 8 Genesis reading">Apollo 8 Genesis reading</a>
      </div> 
      <p>On 24 December 1968, in what was the most watched television broadcast to that date, the <a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">astronauts</a> <a href="/wiki/William_Anders" title="William Anders">Bill Anders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Lovell" title="Jim Lovell">Jim Lovell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frank_Borman" title="Frank Borman">Frank Borman</a> of <a href="/wiki/Apollo_8" title="Apollo 8">Apollo 8</a> surprised the world with a reading of the Creation from the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Genesis" title="Book of Genesis">Book of Genesis</a> as they orbited the Moon.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Madalyn_Murray_O%27Hair" title="Madalyn Murray O'Hair">Madalyn Murray O'Hair</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Atheist" class="mw-redirect" title="Atheist">atheist</a> activist, filed a lawsuit under the <a href="/wiki/Establishment_Clause_of_the_First_Amendment" class="mw-redirect" title="Establishment Clause of the First Amendment">Establishment Clause of the First Amendment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-aldrin_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aldrin-61">[61]</a></sup> The trial court dismissed the lawsuit, which was upheld on appeal.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1969, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Postal_Service" title="United States Postal Service">United States Postal Service</a> issued a stamp (<a href="/wiki/Scott_number" class="mw-redirect" title="Scott number">Scott#</a> 1371) commemorating the Apollo 8 flight around the Moon. The stamp featured a detail of the famous photograph, <i><a href="/wiki/Earthrise" title="Earthrise">Earthrise</a></i>, of the Earth "rising" over the Moon (NASA image AS8-14-2383HR), taken by Anders on Christmas Eve, and the words, "In the beginning God...". </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christmas_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFVaicekauskas2014" class="citation web cs1">Vaicekauskas, Arūnas (2014). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20170722055318/https://eltalpykla.vdu.lt/bitstream/id/3713/9786094670176_2016.pdf">"Ancient Lithuanian Calendar Festivals"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">22 December</span> 2018</span>. <q>The cult of the dead is well noticed in the custom when, after Christmas Eve supper the table is not cleared but left overnight.
